#  [](/thread/222729-trendline-breakouts)Trendline breakouts

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar39895_7.gif) emacro](emacro)

  * | Joined May 2007  | Status: Trader | [640 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=39895)

Trendlines are significant in any timeframe.  
  
3 touches of any trendline and subsequent breakout should see a retest of the breakout and then the start of another trend.  
  
As of current time, eurusd on the 60 min sees possibility of a trend (in the 30 min timeframe) upwards from current levels.  
  
Now that the 60 m trend is up how do we play it?  
  
1 Enter on retrace to the breakout level or just above it  
2 Enter 1/2 position now, then scale in when the market retraces to the breakout point.  
3 Trading trends the stop loss should be larger 100 ticks and over. Just make sure $ risk is 2% of trading account. Aggressive traders can take positions 1 standard lot (100k) per 10K in the account.  
4 The 18 simple moving average provide the risk parameters for the trade. If 2 whole candles close below this then it is time to exit.  
  
Let's see how it pans out...

After a valid breakout of the trendline, the price should come back to retest the breakout price level or just above it.  
  
Note that the long trade is still valid, unless the stop is hit or there are two bars below the 18 sma line. That will be the condition to exit. Remember that we are trading this 60 min trend. For trend trading there needs to be a lot more room given.  
  
Have to knock off to bed now.(2am here) See you on Monday.  
  
Cheers

> Disliked

> Great trades. I consider trendline as pure price action trading.

>  How do you determine the take profit targets?
> 
> Ignored

As one trader once told me, "Entries are dime a dozen and easy to execute, but the real money is made in the exit"  
  
Since this is a trend trade (in the 60 min timeframe) we utilise a trailing stop using the 18 sma. 2 bars closing entirely below this sma indicates an exit. That way one can 'ride the trend'. But, it doesn't preclude you to take partial profits at 'psych levels' the 00s 50s etc... dependent on trade plan.  
  
Cheers  
PS I am expecting 1.3800 as a good level to close the trade...

  * | Joined May 2007  | Status: Trader | [640 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=39895)

> [Quoting shr5](/thread/post/3513079#post3513079 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> sorry for being a lil bit slow but what does "high print" mean technically? thanks in advance  
>    
>  Regards  
>    
>  Ali
> 
> Ignored

There's no such thing as a stupid question...  
  
Means high price quoted. In the old days of stock markets, the prices came over in ticker tape. Prices were printed onto rolling tape, hence if the trade was done at the high, hence the word 'high print'

Cable rebounds through a new trendline.... Jim Rogers who predicted "[The pound will collapse within weeks](http://media.einnews.com/article.php?pid=73800)" will have some sleepless nights this weekend.... We need more of these billionaires to share his dough around...  
  
I actually want to highlight and emphasize to treat such expert oinion in the popular media or cnbc or bloomberg tv as entertainment, no more no less. As Dr Alexander Elder says, "The popular media only reports on stuff that they more or less 100% certain to be true" In this case the huge move in cable downwards. They are news organisations and are in the business of being 'right'. Hence they always report on a commodity or instrument at advanced stages or exhaustion pahse of the move.

> Ignored

In my opinion, the entry depends on your individual trade plan, which reflects your personality. If you decide to enter on break of the TL without a 'close' of the 60 min candle, just bear in mind it can reverse before following through.  
  
I like to let the candle close then enter on retracement. In the 60m timeframe, we are expecting a larger 'trend' to develop, so it is ok to enter late i guess.

> [Quoting bun888](/thread/post/3526278#post3526278 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I understand.  
>  Yes, I figured that a decision should be made after the candle close.  
>  In your experience, is it possible for a trendline to be broken and the next candle came back to the previously broken trendline?
> 
> Ignored

Yes, that happens. There are situations where the candle pokes through the TL and the very same candle closes below. That is also a signal to go the other way...  
  
Remember that markets don't go straight up or down. Inevitably after the breakout and close above/below a TL there is some sort of retracement.

>  and that it is not a busted breakout?

Actually when te trend started and when it ends will only become apparent after the whole trend is finished.  
  
In this case we are assuming a break of the trendline.(preferably 3 touches) However whether the trend continues no one knows, only time will tell.

  * [#64](/thread/post/3544603#post3544603 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 12, 2010 11:33am  Mar 12, 2010 11:33am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31339_6.gif) FXEZ](fxez)

  * Joined Jan 2007 | Status: developing... | [974 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31339)

I offer the following by way of critique of commonly held TA assumptions that everybody takes for granted and not as a critique of your efforts. Please carry on.   
  
Common TA assumptions should be scrutinized by anybody who wants to trade with the probabilities. Ask the following question, how can 2 or 3 data points determine a trend? What about all the other data points - are they less significant than the ones that are cherry picked for trend line drawing? How about another question, why must a trend line be a straight line?  
  

> Quote
> 
> Disliked
> 
> A trend cannot be derived from two points. Two consecutive days of cold weather dont constitute global (or even local) cooling. A trend requires a statistically significant number of observations, and as such we will determine a minimum number of observations to give us statistical significance. Most traditional TA fails by this rule because it allows for the connection of two points into a line, called a trend line with the inference that the connection of two data points defines a support or resistance area.

  
There are lots of other basic TA assumptions that need to be revisited. Many of them are detailed in the post linked below.  
  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...58&postcount=3](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=3534758&postcount=3)  
  

> [Quoting emacro](/thread/post/3500742#post3500742 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Trendlines are significant in any timeframe.  
>    
>  3 touches of any trendline and subsequent breakout should see a retest of the breakout and then the start of another trend.
> 
> Ignored

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

....like the big hitters Soros and Rogers,....there is nobody left to buy the US Dollar.  
  
This week we will lay off the 'Jim Rogers' bashing...  
The dailyfx.com report entitled "[US dollar at risk for further weakness v euro on FX positioning."](http://www.dailyfx.com/forex/fundamental/forecast/weekly/usd/2010-03-12-2259-US_Dollar_at_Risk_for.html)  
  
The most poignant wording in this report are:  
"In recent months we have argued that the US Dollar was likely to recover against the Euro and other key counterparts on extremely one-sided bearish positioning and sentiment. Yet the tables have clearly turned in the Dollars favor; CFTC Commitment of Traders data shows Non-Commercials at a record net-long the US currency against the Euro. Such one-sided USD-bullish positioning has made it extremely difficult for the currency to eke out further gains. Indeed, a further unwind would almost certainly bring EURUSD rallies."

#  [](/thread/222729-trendline-breakouts)Trendline breakouts 

  * 

  * [#101](/thread/post/3562808#post3562808 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 18, 2010 7:28pm  Mar 18, 2010 7:28pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar101502_3.gif) Far East Man](far*east*man)

  * | Joined May 2009  | Status: Trader | [52 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=101502)

> [Quoting MarketPips](/thread/post/3561777#post3561777 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> After how many pips of break do you count it as a breakout?
> 
> Ignored

He hasn't clearly mentioned about how many pips the price actually has to pass over the line. He waits for the price to retrace back to the breakout point to place an entry, so the amount of price buffer may not be a big issue for him.  
  
Although I personally tend to enter on an initial breakout, the advantage of emacro's strategy is that he doesn't pick the initial breakout, and just let the market breath and wait for a pull back so that you can safely enter into a trade after identifying a real breakout has occurred or not.  
  
Hope it helps. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Have been thoroughly enjoying this site. Was wondering why MACD histogram only is used instead of the complementary slow and fast moving average lines also? As oftentimes, divergence may appear on one and not the other?  
Good investing!

> 
> Disliked
> 
> Have been thoroughly enjoying this site. Was wondering why MACD histogram only is used instead of the complementary slow and fast moving average lines also? As oftentimes, divergence may appear on one and not the other?  
>  Good investing!
> 
> Ignored

Glad you are enjoying the read...  
  
Macd histogram helps give an indication of the momentum. If present then it helps if not, then the momentum is not behind the trade. That still doesn't mean things won't work out.  
  
Feel free to contribute to the discussion.

> He hasn't clearly mentioned about how many pips the price actually has to pass over the line. He waits for the price to retrace back to the breakout point to place an entry, so the amount of price buffer may not be a big issue for him.  
>    
>  Although I personally tend to enter on an initial breakout, the advantage of emacro's strategy is that he doesn't pick the initial breakout, and just let the market breath and wait for a pull back so that you can safely enter into a trade after identifying a real breakout has occurred or not.  
>    
>  Hope it helps.
> 
> Ignored

Basically this is a discretionary method, no hard and fast rule. If you notice in the last m5 cable example, the candle that pierced the trendline was a big one. That is also a contributing factor.  
  
The main point is to have your trade strategy and plan set out. Whether to do like Far East Man, jump in on penetration or to enter on retrace, that depends on your trade plan, which will reflect your personality.(hopefully)  
  
Cheers 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * Mar 22, 2010 6:09pm  Mar 22, 2010 6:09pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar39895_7.gif) emacro](emacro)

  * | Joined May 2007  | Status: Trader | [640 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=39895)

Before anyone asks, the green and white bars represent when momentum and inertia of the market in that timeframe are pointing in the same direction:  
  
Momentum=MACD Histogram standard settings  
Inertia=13 ema  
  
This is Dr Elder's 'Impulse Momentum' system in his book, "Come into my trading room".

Hi Far East Man  
  
Thanks for the heads up. I am ony just starting today to look at the charts.  
  
I'd wait for the Macd histogram to hook up then can go long eurusd. By the time it hook up, momentum is in your favour (at least) and the level you enter might just end up being approx what you enter by catching the falling knife.  
  
But if you want to enter on the retrace to the pullback level, it is still ok, as long the risk management stop you can stomach.

> [Quoting Le Loup](/thread/post/3583268#post3583268 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Can you also trade this system using the 15min chart or is it more effective in the 60min chart?
> 
> Ignored

It's just trendline breaks, support and resistance points being broken. I guess you can use 15 min as trigger, but 5 min is good to trigger the trade, once the 60 min shows heads up. For example, today the 60 min showed a divergence, which as Dr Alexander Elder describes, "The most powerful signal in technical analysis..."

> [Quoting larry x](/thread/post/3626036#post3626036 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> @Emarco great thread you have going here..i dont know if it has been mentioned before but i would like a clarification.Is it there always a retest of previous trend level for every breakout??How do we know if there wont be a retest??while waiting for a retest and it doesnt come do we let the trade go and wait for another oppotunity?thanks mate.
> 
> Ignored

As with all facets related to trading, one must balance tradeoffs between risk and reward. If you jump in without waiting for retest then your risk is greater and reward commensurate. A retest trade will make the risk lower but the momentum may have waned resulting in lass rewarding gain. With daily charts though as in last week's eurjpy trade there is ample time to make the decision.  
  
How you choose to trade depends on your own personality, risk tolerance etc and your trading plan.  
  
Cheers

#  [](/thread/222729-trendline-breakouts)Trendline breakouts

  * [#181](/thread/post/3636621#post3636621 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 14, 2010 4:06pm  Apr 14, 2010 4:06pm 

  * [ G-Man](g-man)

  * | Joined Mar 2006  | Status: Trader | [423 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=7111)

Nice thread on trendlines emacro. Does raise a few questions on your mehtodolgy but I'll start with just a quick one.  
  
After the TL break, do you have a set time for the retracement to form? For example, is the next bar after the close below counted as a valid retrace or is it considered too early. Conversely, is there an extended period of time, say 12 bars, after the break that you would not consider taking the retrace trade.  
  
Thanks in advance and keep posting the charts. Very interesting.  
  
G-Man 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#182](/thread/post/3640014#post3640014 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 15, 2010 1:14pm  Apr 15, 2010 1:14pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar39895_7.gif) emacro](emacro)

  * | Joined May 2007  | Status: Trader | [640 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=39895)

> [Quoting G-Man](/thread/post/3636621#post3636621 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Nice thread on trendlines emacro. Does raise a few questions on your mehtodolgy but I'll start with just a quick one.  
>    
>  After the TL break, do you have a set time for the retracement to form? For example, is the next bar after the close below counted as a valid retrace or is it considered too early. Conversely, is there an extended period of time, say 12 bars, after the break that you would not consider taking the retrace trade.  
>    
>  Thanks in advance and keep posting the charts. Very interesting.  
>    
>  G-Man
> 
> Ignored

After the breakout, we assume the resistance now becomes support. So there is no time limit, although some would argue that the longer the elapsed time, the less valid the new support is.  
  
Sometimes, the faster the retrace the faster the move off the s/r level and vice versa, as per Newton's laws of motion....  
  
Cryptic I know but trading and chart reading is more art than science.  
  
Cheers 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#197](/thread/post/3667950#post3667950 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 25, 2010 12:37am  Apr 25, 2010 12:37am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar39895_7.gif) emacro](emacro)

  * | Joined May 2007  | Status: Trader | [640 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=39895)

> [Quoting ukcool](/thread/post/3667927#post3667927 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi Emacro,   
>    
>  What our your rules for the 5min trendline breaks.
> 
> Ignored

In the first post.  
  
Bear in mind that there is a bit of discretion to use these shorter time frame tl breaks. We need the bigger picture eg divergence, or trendline break in the 60 min or daily, then drilling down to 5 min, 12 min or lower timeframe, one can look for trendline breaks to enter in the direction on bigger tf. You can also dispense with these shorter timeframes and just trade off 60 min.  
  
In short, look for a bias or direction on bigger tf, then drill down to 5 min for the tl break to enter.(and try to trade in direction of momentum, green and white bars which is just the ema/macd histogram pointing in the same direction) 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Hence there is no hard and fast data on win% etc, because it is not mechanical.

Best of luck and inform forumers how it goes.

  * May 4, 2010 12:19pm  May 4, 2010 12:19pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar39895_7.gif) emacro](emacro)

> [Quoting Le Loup](/thread/post/3692024#post3692024 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> How do you draw your trendlines? I mean, do you have any rules on which points to connect?
> 
> Ignored

  
Some discretion involved. 3 or more touches makes a trendline more valid.

  * May 18, 2010 4:41pm  May 18, 2010 4:41pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar39895_7.gif) emacro](emacro)

  * | Joined May 2007  | Status: Trader | [640 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=39895)

Would like to put some thoughts for new traders to consider in money management.  
  
Starting capital $50000  
divide by 50=$1000 per day maximum loss limit  
limit losses to a maximum of $400 per standard lot traded  
  
With that formula in place you can then at least last 50 days. When one trades and starts out, one needs the ability to be in the game long enough to learn and hopefully fine tune your system to be profitable in the long run.  
  
Remember, to get from $1 to $1m is not 1 step, but you must count $1 $2 $3 $4 and so on to hopefully eventually get to $1m.

  * May 18, 2010 9:27pm  May 18, 2010 9:27pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar39895_7.gif) emacro](emacro)

  * | Joined May 2007  | Status: Trader | [640 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=39895)

It has been an interesting few weeks since this thread has started. I enjoy the experience of having my own thread.  
  
Although I think it has not been that popular a thread, I hope that it has helped some to understand the concept of using trendlines as support/resistance, to delineate a 'line in the sand' between uptrends and downtrends.  
  
With that, this will be my last post for a while at least.   
  
Cheers to all

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar148722_2.gif) Mortician.](mortician.)

  * | Additional Username  | Joined Jul 2010 | [225 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=148722)

> [Quoting FXEZ](/thread/post/3544603#post3544603 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I offer the following by way of critique of commonly held TA assumptions that everybody takes for granted and not as a critique of your efforts. Please carry on.   
>    
>  Common TA assumptions should be scrutinized by anybody who wants to trade with the probabilities. Ask the following question, how can 2 or 3 data points determine a trend? What about all the other data points - are they less significant than the ones that are cherry picked for trend line drawing? How about another question, why must a trend line be a straight line?  
>    
>    
>    
>  There are...
> 
> Ignored

I will address your question.  
  
How can 2 or 3 data points determine a trend?  
  
ANS: Well, the minimum you need to determine a trend are two data points. You cannot use one data point. You need at least two. This is mathematics. Now, for a given sample size, two may or may not be enough. It all depends on what you are looking for, what function you are using to plot these two data points together, what is the statistics noise level, etc. But just because you have two data points doesnt mean it is meaningless.  
  
Also, the presupposition that you have two or 48 data points is simply contextual. That is, it all depends on the timeframe. Using the daily chart, a single data point is 1, but zoom to hourly chart, that same single data point suddenly becomes 24 data points. Since you've converted daily to 24hourly data. You can to this for monthly vs 1hour. In that sense a single monthly data point suddenly becomes an 720 data points(24hours X 30 days). As such, a 1, 2, 3 data points are all in the eyes of the beholder.  
  
Why is a trendline a straightline?  
  
ANS: In algebra, to draw a line you need at least two points. All algrebaic lines are straight. So, why wont a trading system(trendlines) based on algebraic concept of lines be straight? Of course, it will be straight. Trendlines are straight because they are based on algebraic concept of lines which are themselves straight. Unless you want to challenge the foundational concept of mathematics that derives straightlines.   
  
Not to get really off topic, even curves and circles are straight lines when you use differential calculus limit/exhaustion method. dy/dx.  
  
That said, any trend determining mechanics doesnt have to be a straight line: moving averages, elliot waves, series of swing highs/lows, etc. all these can determine a trend. But asking why is a trendline a straight line is like asking why is elliot waves a wave or why is moving averages averages. It makes no sense. the nature of trendline is to be a line, and lines are straight otherwise they wont be a line. Asking why a line is straight is meaningless, trendlines are lines, they have to be straight, otherwise, they wont be a line. This is axiomatic. This is a mathematical axiom. It is the same as asking why is a curve a curve or why is a triangle a triangle or rectangle a rectangle. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Very good answers, well done.  
  
As prices derived from the auction process (market) are the end result of supply and demand form market participants, there is an inherent randomness and hence madness to market prices. By using assumptions and orderly structures such as trendlines and TA, one can get (hopefully) a more cognisant picture on which to make buy and sell decisions.

> [Quoting sk_255](/thread/post/4009965#post4009965 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> hi emacro   
>    
>  how do you know which direction to draw the trendline in order for it to break up or down? does it matter? do you consider larger timeframes when you draw your trendlines? when i look at your charts it looks so obvious but when i look at mine i dont know where to start!
> 
> Ignored

Sorry for the late reply.  
  
The trendline is a 'line in the sand' between having a bullish bias or bearish bias. Say you choose the higher timeframe as 30 min (as in CAD futures attached) the larger timeframe 30m is showing bearish bias, so on lower timeframe trigger like 1 min etc you'd try to draw the trendline to go with the direction of the higher timeframe bias from which side of any trendline drawn.  
  
Note: bottom chart 1 min top chart 30min  
  
Hope it helps.  
  
Cheers

After a lot of good info on this thread i'like to give my contribution to this forum....here is an indicator alert to help you treading Break out TL:

> Please whats the rule or principle for Drawing ur TrendLine?

> Ignored

It's discretionary. The trendlines provide a bull/bear barrier, and as with all, the higher timeframe would be more of a 'fit', but then any trade has higher risk on higher timeframes.

  * Dec 18, 2012 2:53am  Dec 18, 2012 2:53am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar67941_5.gif) big_pipin](big_pipin)

  * Joined Apr 2008 | Status: Trader | [1,230 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=67941)

The problem with your tl's is that:  
  
1\. TL's in general are very subjective based on where you draw the starting point.  
  
2\. Secondly, you're tl's are so short term in nature that they have not been well tested.  
  
I've tried for a long time to trade breaks but its one of the hardest strategies. Breaks fail more often then they succeed, which brings be to a few more questions.  
  
1\. Looks like you're going long on the pull backs?.. why?..if most breaks fail, why are you not shorting the pops and at least covering at the retest of the tl?  
  
would be nice to see you post entries on these charts when they occur and update them with exit prices.  
  
Anyone can throw up charts.

> Quote
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I've tried for a long time to trade breaks but its one of the hardest strategies.

  
Yes, that's right. Some traders are thinking that breakout is easy to trade compare with trend following.  
But it is exact opposite - it is difficult to trade. It is easy to see it on the chart (post-breakout) but it is not easy to trade using price action only (sr and tl only).

  * | Joined Oct 2005  | Status: Trader | [35 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=4010)

well.  
do you know why it is so difficult to trade on this way?  
  
Because trendlines and support/resistance lines are indicating the following: what is going with the price right now.  
Right now on open bar.  
It is very different from standard indicators because we are trading indicators on close (means: previous) bar.  
And trendlines - on open bar; it means: the situation is changed every moment in case of trendlines.

> 
> Disliked
> 
> I think emacro is correct (read first post of this thread):
> 
> Ignored

I agree the trendlines are very subjective, hence the 'art' in tech analysis.  
  
The breaks are a reason to trade. What we want to do is to try to get aboard a trend and 'let it run'. The timeframe however will determine how long it can potentially last.  
  
No method is 90% or 100%, and at some point, all technical methods will fail. Moves like the eurjpy 1hr will hopefully enable the trader to cover some failed breakout trades. It is good to have others say their mind on whether a method is crap or not, as everyone is entitled to their opinion.  
  
Anyway Crude Oil is on its way.

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar4010_2.gif) newdigital](newdigital)

I name it "ready to go"  la Warcraft ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
  

Attached Image

![](/attachment/image/1101662?d=1355809283)

  
  
  
What does it mean?  
When all support/resistance lines and tl came very close to each other with the price in the middle so ... we can expect breakout soon. Price is telling to you: "ready to go"  
  
=======

So, it is metatrader statement.  
I opened first trade for USDJPY yesterday (see some my previous post on this thread), and finished the trading few hours ago.  
  
  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: trendlines.gif
Size: 5 KB](/attachment/image/1102089/thumbnail?d=1365805364)](/attachment/image/1102089?d=1355849046)   

  
  
  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: tl_workplace.jpg
Size: 334 KB](/attachment/image/1102088/thumbnail?d=1365805364)](/attachment/image/1102088?d=1355849046)   

  
  
Metatrader statement is attached to this post (in rar archive).  
  
Please find attached the second indicator I am using: MaksiGen_Range_Move mtf 2.  
And template is attached too.  
  
How to install.  
\- Place MaksiGen_Range_Move mtf 2 indicator (attached to this post) and Maksigen indicator (see link below to download) to indicators folder of Metatrader directory (for example, to C![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f61c.png?v=15.1)rogram Files - MetaTrader - Alpari - experts - indicators);  
\- place template file (attached to this post) to template folder (for example, to C![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f61c.png?v=15.1)rogram Files - MetaTrader - Alpari - templates);  
\- compile indicators to MetaEditor, or restart Metatrader;  
\- open M1 chart, right mouse click on the chart, select our template - indicators will be loaded to the chart. And you can practise for example.  
  
Please note: M1 timeframe is used just to practise only.  
I am using M1 timeframe for trading s/r/tl but using M1 timeframe - looks like trading pure price action without indicators (means: it is difficult and required some experience). But it is really good practise for the people who want to understand about trendlines.   
  
After that you can reply to very simple question: "hi guys, it seems breakout is good but what is it all about?" ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
That's all news  
  
  
=======

  * [#391](/thread/post/6307176#post6307176 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 19, 2012 5:02pm  Dec 19, 2012 5:02pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar4010_2.gif) newdigital](newdigital)

  * | Joined Oct 2005  | Status: Trader | [35 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=4010)

> [Quoting wanaxau](/thread/post/6306826#post6306826 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> i've seen your trading statement, one question, how to setup and manage our Take Profit and StopLoss ? I see all your trading closed, some trade differ than take profit or stoploss. Thank you.
> 
> Ignored

In case of trading manually - I am always trying to use stop loss. And I am using take profit sometimes. When I am trading manually so I can open one trade .. after that - I can re-enter on same pair (after reversal for example). Because of that (many trades are kept to be opened on the same time) I try to close the trades based on the situation ... and the situation (especially for M1 timeframe) are changed all the time. Besides - I am closing the trades based on margins ... if the price is going against me so I am trying to close some trades with small profit to avoid margin call ... besides, I do not want to receive big floating drawdown because as we know - market was not going in fully trend following way yesterday - it was some ranging time as well.  
  
To make it shorter - there are many trading styles (in case of trading manually):  
\- classical trading style (one trade per pair only; next trade will not be opened untill old trade is closed)  
\- re-entering  
...  
...  
and so on  
  
So, I am using re-enter - re-enter is the term which was originally used in AscTrend software made by american AbleSys Corp, and this term was used by many traders and coders after that in Russia and everywhere. But as I remember - this re-enter trading style came from Ichimoku so it's Japanese originally

When I am trading manually so I can open one trade .. after that - I can re-enter on same pair (after reversal for example). Because of that (many trades are kept to be opened on the same time) I try to close the trades based on the situation ... and the situation (especially for M1 timeframe) are changed all the time. Besides - I am closing the trades based on margins ... if the price is going against me so I am trying to close some trades...
> 
> Ignored

>

> And for your re-entry position, where i can find reference to make re-entry position like you

> Ignored

About re-enter ...  
It is something what I explained for some other forum.  
  
it is classical way of trend following trading (1 trade per chart/pair in trend following way):  
  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: classicalwayoftrading_1.jpg
Size: 223 KB](/attachment/image/1102842/thumbnail?d=1365805618)](/attachment/image/1102842?d=1355937904)   

  
  
It is classical way of trend following trading with re-enter:  
  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: classical_and_reenter_nonscalping_2.jpg
Size: 232 KB](/attachment/image/1102843/thumbnail?d=1365805618)](/attachment/image/1102843?d=1355937904)   

  
  
It is classical way of trading with scalping re-enter:  
  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: classical_and_reenter_scalping_3.jpg
Size: 228 KB](/attachment/image/1102850/thumbnail?d=1365805618)](/attachment/image/1102850?d=1355938169)   

  
  
  
This trading style (re-enter) was hard coded for some trading platform (very very long time ago; not for metatrader) with exact this word - 're-enter'. Means: we are having the main trade/order, and we are "playing" inside this trade/direction by openning/re-entering. Scalping in this way is the same re-enter but without the main trade/order.  
There is counter trend style as well but it is something similar: there is main trade/order (or without it if in pure scalping way), and re-enter is made in counter trend way (in opposite direction to the main trend/trade).  
  
Difference between classical styles and pure scalping is the following:  
\- in classical way with re-enter - the main trade/order should be opened;  
\- in pure scalping way/style - we are trading without openning the main trade/order just making re-enters (in trend following way, or in counter trend way) taking onto consideration this main trend.  
  
=======  
  
_\- MaksiGen indicator is on[this post](http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=222729&page=25) (indicator is drawing s/r/tl depends on preselected number of bars).  
\- MTrendLine alert indicator is on [this post](http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=6303470#post6303470).  
\- __MaksiGen_Range_Move mtf 2 indicator is on[this post](http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=6305334#post6305334).  
\- Template to trade or monitor M1 timeframe is on [this post](http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=6305334#post6305334)._

yes, except "star" and "cross" marks which I made manually on the chart.  
Maksigen indicator is having the settings ... did you see vertical lines on the chart? Attach Maksigen indicator with default settngs - and you will see. Name of those parameters? Move your mouse to any of this vertical line - and you will see the name of the parameter in indicator. Those lines are the bars. Maksigen indicator is drawing support/resistance lines (trend line is one of them) calculated for some number of bars. So, if you change the settings in indicator - you will receive different s/r/tls calculated based on different bars.  
  
There are some indicators with re-enter (coded by Igorad - ask him please) but I did not use them in trading here.  
In my trading here - I used exact template which I uploaded here.
